<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="maturation">Maturation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>HIV uses the part of the cell outer membrane to complete its final structure. The new HIV particles leave the cell in search of new cell to infect and start the process again.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-stage-in-hiv">Clinical stage in HIV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-stage-in-hiv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Modes and non modes of transmission of sexually transmitted disease and infection</p>
<p>HIV transmission is the spread of HIV virus from one person to another by different routes. HIV is spread when an infected individual comes into contact with infected body fluids or cells. The virus is found in blood, breast milk, semen and virginal secretion. In high concentration and saliva in low conclusion</p>

<p>HIV can be transmitted through various modes sexual contact - the commonest mode, any unprotected penetration sex whether virginal, anal or oral can transmit the virus from an infected individual to uninfected.</p>
<p>Sexual contact accounts for 70-80 percent transmission. Homosexual accounts for 10-15% HIV infection by sexually account for between 1-3%.</p>
<p>Oral sex is associated with a lower risk but gonorrhea and genital cancer and syphilis do but the risk of transmission.</p>
<p>Deep kissing weak 'oral saliva is exchanged causes some risk of HIV transmission especially when one or both partners have bleeding gums, shivering of tooth brush and toothpicks have small risk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-influencing-the-risk-of-hiv-transmission">Factors influencing the risk of HIV transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-the-risk-of-hiv-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>No of sexual partners. The higher the number off sexual partners one has the higher the chances of contracting HIV.</li>
<li>The level of virus in the body fluid. The higher level of risk in body fluid (blood, semen, virginal secretion) the higher the risk of transmission.</li>
<li>Sexual orientation. Being homosexual, homo sexual or unprotected sex influence a great deal of HIV transmission, unprotected guys sex causes great risk.</li>
<li>Gender. the chances of a woman contracting the virus from an infected man is statistically higher than the chances of uninfected man can contract the virus s from an infected woman.</li>
<li>Age. Younger women are at higher risk as opposed to other women this is because during sexual intercourse virginal tissue tears and get fractured because they are not fully developed.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Sexually transmitted disease. Presence of STDS increases chances of HIV infection because they cause ulcer and lesions that open up the skin.</li>
<li>Mother to child transmission disease. World wide rate of HIV infection from mother to their children ran from 13-40% i.e. 4% out of 10% children born to HIV positive e mothers contract HIV.</li>
</ol>
<p>Ways of mother to child transmission</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i) The child can be infected before birth by virus crossing from the mother blood to the child through placenta. About 35% of newly born infant which are HIV infected at birth.</p>
<p>ii) The child can contract HIV through exposure to mother blood and other expulsion during birth. This account for about 05% of newly born HIV infected at birth is most of mother to child transmission occur during birth.</p>
<p>iii) The child can contract HIV positive mother that get infected with HIV contract virus as a result of breast feeding.</p>

<p>By the end of this topic the learner should be in a position to;</p>
<ul>
<li>Define sexually transmitted infection</li>

<p>Sexually transmitted infection (STDs) vulnerable group of disease or infection whose predominant mode of transmission is through sexual intercourse</p>
<p>Stds makes one more vulnerable to HIV infection e.g. gonorrhea and genital herpes thus early treatment to aspect of HIV infection.</p>
<p>When one is infected by STDs he/ she depict the following symptoms</p>
<ul>
<li>Urethral discharge</li>
<li>Virginal discharge</li>
<li>Genital ulcers</li>
<li>Long abdominal pain</li>
<li>Eye infection in newborn</li>
<li>Swelling of scrotum</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples of STDs</p>
<p>Gonorrhea</p>
<p>Causative agent</p>
<ul>
<li>Neisseria gonococcus</li>
</ul>
<p>Signs</p>
<ul>
<li>Burning when passing urine</li>
<li>Discharge of pus through the urethra of the virginal or sore growth in case of oral sex,</li>
</ul>
<p>Complication and treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>Damage of fallopian duct in female and epididymis in male leading to sterility</li>
<li>Inflammation of joint, liver, heart and peritoneum may occur.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment By use of effective antibiotic as the organism is resistant to several times. Noflocin is a useful antibiotic.</p>

Signs and symptoms</p>

<li>Burning in the virginal and urethra</li>
<li>Greenish – yellow discharge</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complication-and-treatment">Complication and treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complication-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="candidiasis">Candidiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#candidiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Causative agent – a fungus called Candida albicans
Signs and symptoms</p>
<ul>
<li>Burning in the virginal and the urethra</li>
<li>White thick discharge sometimes tiredness with blood.</li>
</ul>
<p>Complication and treatment</p>
<p>May lead to pre cancer condition of the neck and womb (cervix cancer)</p>
<p>Treated with anti fungalpassure or cream e.g. doctrimazole.</p>
<p>GENITAL Herpes.</p>
<p>Causative agent</p>
<p>Herpes simplex agent</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms</p>
<p>Painful vascular rushes in the genitals</p>
<p>Complication and treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>Figia damage unborn baby eventually treating to death.</li>
<li>Cancer of the neck of the womb no nearly the effective treatment.</li>
<li>Acyclorin may be harmful.</li>
</ul>
<p>HEPATITIS</p>
<p>Causative agent</p>
<p>Hepatitis ‘B’ virus</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms</p>
<p>Yellow less of eyes (juridical) due to liver damage</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain around right upper abdomen</li>
<li>Lead to cancer of the liver.</li>
</ul>
<p>Complication and treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>Cancer of the liver.</li>
<li>No treatment, vaccine, available also transmitted by blood transfusion.</li>
</ul>
<p>AIDS</p>
<p>Causative agent HIV</p>
<p>Signs</p>
<p>Many different signs but dominated by weight less and opportunistic infections.</p>
<p>Complication and treatment</p>
<p>Much complication eventually leading to death i.e. no cure</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relationship-between-stds-and-hiv-aids">Relationship between STDS and HIV AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relationship-between-stds-and-hiv-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>In both of them the victim should always be educated on ways of avoiding re infection for it will worsen the situation</li>

<li>Advance disease</li>
</ol>
<p>Transmission stage</p>
<p>Transmission of HIV/AIDS with the 1st stage without, with non of the subsequent stage can occur</p>
<ul>
<li>Basically HIV virus is transmitted through contact with body fluids e.g sexual intercourse. accounting 80% of HIV transmission intravenous drug use 10% unscreened blood transfusion accounting 5% of HIV transmission and exposure to contaminated instrument accounting 0.1% e.g. needle. Mother to child transmission accounting 10% of HIV transmission.</li>
<li>Primary injection. The symptoms of injection occur normally 2-6 weeks after exposure to the virus. In 50-80% of patient the symptom are normally mild and patient might dismiss them as mild through symptoms. this might be accompanied by swelling of the glands, sore throats which may persist up to 14 days. CD4 will decline as immune system come into attack from the virus but will recover as the immune system land to fight injection through production of antibodies.</li>
</ul>
<p>Antibodies may become detectable 10-14 days after the onset of symptoms however depending on the sensitivity of the test and level of A HIV test may still be negative once natural viral suppression due to immune function occur the level of virus reaches a plateau 3-6 months after the injection has taken place.</p>
<p>Its during zero conversion that the patient is tightly infectious and transmission of virus is very likely while viral level remains high in the body fluids.</p>
<p>The plateau in the viral level is called viral sets.</p>
<p>Point and may indicate this rate of viral replication e.g. disease progression is likely to be faster in those in those with high viral subsequent.</p>
<p>ASSYMPTOMATIC PHASE</p>
<p>During the phase the patient remain asymptomatic (no signs of HIV / aids) although enlarged gland may characterize the phase with minor complication which the patients ignore as not no medical attention. Oral lesion may be represented as ulcers and the patients may have increased sinuses and other respiratory tract.</p>
<p>Many patients may take this normal cause infection if they are unaware of their status and treat with over the counter medicine.</p>

<p>Here cd4 count has fallen below 500 and remain above 200. Patients begin manifesting symptom of HIV / aids and may develop a risk of bacteria pneumonias or, pulmonary TB. Also during this stage mouth infection may also show itself as oral thrush and oral leukoplakia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advanced-disease">ADVANCED DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advanced-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During this stage the cd4 counts fails below 200 patients may develop a variety of opportunistic infection of which include</p>
<ul>
<li>Non-pulmonary TB</li>
<li>Pneumocytic pneumonia and may be accompanied by weight loss, fatigue and extreme headache and the patient may sometime become bad ridden. As the CD4 count drop below 50. The condition?</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="negative-impact">Negative impact<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#negative-impact" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>High dropout of student especially for girls who take care of sick at home</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ A large proportion of funds are ghptowards recruitment of new staff to replace the weak and the dying staff.
✓ The rate of absenteeism for teachers and staff is high i.e. it reduces lab our productivity</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-industry-and-trade-sector">2. Industry and trade sector<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-industry-and-trade-sector" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Loss of productivity due to reduced labour</p>
<p>Reduces capacity for investment as resources are channeled towards the treatment and care of the sick employees</p>

<p>INTRODUCTIONS</p>
<p>The body has a two –part Immune system which workers together to protect it from harmful micro organism such as bacteria, fungi, viruses and parasites, it is divided in to two:</p>
<p>Innate Immunity</p>
<p>This is the front-line defense which equips us from before birth to deal with the various microorganisms that we are likely to meet in our normal everyday lives</p>
<p>Innate Immunity Include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antibodies formed by a mother and passed on to the developing foetus and through infant breasting feeding</li>
</ul>
<p>Tears containing the enzyme lysosome, to protect one eye from bacteria</p>
<p>Saliva in the mouth, also containing the anti-bacterial lysosome</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Mucus and chemicals co-existing but with quite differing functions in the urethra Uretes (water tubes) and vagina</p>
<p>When the barriers of the innate immunity are penetrated, while blood cells leukocyte. (phagocytes or devouring cells) and other while cells (principally serotoxin or natural cell-killing cells) surround and a number of other naturally-produced substances such as interfere and a range of blood proteins (called the complement system combine to help in the destruction process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adaptive-immunity">Adaptive Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adaptive-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Adaptive Immunity is the second line of defense and is called into service when the defenses of the innate immunity are breached well beyond the capability of its response. Its defense, instead of being a general reaction is much more specific as it adapts to the particular organism present hence adaptive immunity is often referred to as specific immune system to identify the invading micro-organism as being foreign to any of the body’s own protein (these foreign or devouring cells) and other while cells (principally serotoxin or natural cell-killing cells) surround and attempt to destroy the invader. At the same time a number of other naturally-produced substances such as interferon and a range of blood proteins called the complement system combine to help in the destruction process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adaptive-immunity">Adaptive Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adaptive-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Adaptive Immunity is the second line of defense and is called into service when the defenses of the innate immunity are breached well beyond the capability of it response. It defense, instead of being a general reaction is much more specific as it adapts to the particular organism present hence adaptive immunity is often referred to as specific immunity.</p>
<p>The role of the adaptive immune system to identify the invading micro-organism as being foreign to any of the body own protein (these foreign to any of the body own proteins these foreign protein are called antigens (antibody regenerators) from Greek works meaning against and engender)</p>
<p>The response can be either humeral or cellules based on the type of invade</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="areas-of-counseling">Areas Of counseling.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#areas-of-counseling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The two main areas of HIV counseling are;</p>
<ul>
<li>Educating the infected person so that they will understand the nature of their problems</li>
<li>explanation of the available treatment options; outlining ways to prevent others from being infected by them</li>
<li>Support through anxieties and other physical need meets by people in the cause of their illness.</li>
<li>Counseling opportunities will exist at different stage and provided by different individuals.</li>
<li>Appropriate counseling intervention include</li>
<li>Initial attendance at a clinic or medical centre where the at risk person will have the HIV testing procedures explained.</li>
<li>Personal counseling of the HIV-positive person and the partner family where this is possible and applicable</li>
<li>Available treatment regimes</li>
<li>Instruction is safer sexual practices</li>
<li>Explanation of the development and effect of opportunistic infection and their delay /treatment</li>
<li>Counseling the family of bereaved</li>
<li>Support Networks</li>
<li>Counselors and counseling facilities vary from country to country so there is hardly a standard approach</li>
</ul>
<p>All community agencies should be alert to their opportunities to provide support to the sick in their midst and to help people with HIV/Aids and their dependants.</p>
<p>This network of support will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Families, friends work colleagues</li>
<li>Medical and paramedical staff</li>
</ul>

<p>Prevention and control of HIV /AIDs</p>
<p>HIV prevention services seem to work best when all the stakeholders are involved in implementation of the strategies. In Kenya the Interpersonal donor partners local and international NGO's faith-best organization are involved in activities and service to prevent HIV/Aids</p>
<p>Some of the activities implemented by this organization include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Basic evaluation and dissemination of information about HIV.</li>
<li>Communication about behavior change.</li>
<li>Community mobilization to change social norms</li>
<li>Training youths and adolescent in life skill and behavior change e.g. being assertions responsibility accountability social skill ways of relating to others developing a positive image.</li>
<li>Peer education and youth to youth initiatives</li>
<li>Voluntary counseling and testing (V.C.T)</li>
<li>Prevention and treatment of other sexually transmitted diseases.</li>
<li>Prevention of mother to child transmission</li>
<li>Prevention of transfusion in medical settings including are blood transfusion and proper injection control</li>
<li>Condom education and distribution promotion.</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention and control strategies used in Kenya.</p>
<ol>
<li>V.C.T as a prevention strategy it is a powerful weapon in the fight against HIV/AIDs since it is associated with behavior change that reduces HIV transmission and serves as a point of entry into care for those testing positive through the joint effort of stakeholders</li>
</ol>
<p>There has been rapid increase of V.C.T sites in Kenya in the year 2008</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>V.C.T services are offered through site registration by the ministry of health as an effort to increase the number of people who are tested and to expand access to Aids case and treatment.</p>
<p>The National V.C.T programme use for models of services delivery.</p>
<p>Intergrated-Intergarded sites are V.C.T centre which are located within the ground of health facilities such as hospital health centers or dispensaries. There are main advantages include.</p>
<p>Easier referral to medical care service</p>
<p>Low start up cost that allows for an increasing number of people being tested and accessing AIDs core and treatment.</p>
<p>Short coming of integrated sites includes</p>
<p>Health workers</p>
<p>They may have more urgent medical problems to attend to and cannot develop enough time to VCT</p>
<p>Stand alone sites – This sites are not usually with existing medical Institution usually have staff denoted to V.C.T, They largely operated by NGOs agencies and they usually located at intensely populated urban areas.</p>
<p>Advantages</p>
<p>They staff can work full time on VCT service</p>
<p>They have donor funds that facilitate their community approach site.</p>
<p>Are V.C.T centers either intergraded into other social service or implanted as a souls activity of a local community based organization (CBOS)</p>
<p>Mobile sites</p>
<p>V.C.T services are provided as an outreach to remote to reach communities.</p>
<p>Benefits of V.C.T</p>
<p>Helps in prevention of transmission of HIV serves as a flat form for care and treatment of Aids</p>
<p>Helps in planning for individual organization as well as the government</p>
<p>Help in identifying the number of HIV infected persons and ways of addressing or promoting prevention of transmission</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="question">QUESTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hiv-aids-vulnerable-groups">HIV &amp; AIDS Vulnerable Groups<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-aids-vulnerable-groups" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>AIDS is caused by HIV, a virus that can be passed from person to person through sexual fluids, blood and breast milk.</p>
<p>Worldwide, the majority of HIV infections are transmitted through sex between men and women, and half of all adults living with HIV are women. Certain groups of people have been particularly affected and these include people who inject drugs, sex workers and men who have sex with men.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>HIV particularly affects adolescents and young people, who accounted for 39 percent of all new infections and 15 percent of all people living with HIV in 2012. 1 AIDS-related deaths among young adults have an especially damaging impact on their families and communities: skills are lost, workforces shrink and children are orphaned.</p>
<p>In some countries in sub-Saharan Africa, life expectancies have fallen below 40 years, whereas they would have been above 60 without the epidemic. Roughly 17.8 million children have lost at least one parent to AIDS-related illnesses. 2</p>
<p>Apart from inadequate funding, other major obstacles to reducing the vulnerability of these populations to HIV include weak infrastructure and shortages of healthcare workers in the worst affected countries. Political or cultural attitudes are also significant. For example, some authorities are opposed to condom promotion, while others refuse to support needle exchanges for people who inject drugs. Many are also reluctant to provide young people with adequate education about sex and sexual health.</p>
<p>Stigma and discrimination particularly affects these vulnerable groups. People known to be living with HIV are often shunned or abused by community members, employers even healthcare workers. As well as causing much personal suffering, this sort of prejudice discourages people from seeking HIV testing, treatment and care, undermining efforts to tackle the epidemic.</p>
<p>AIDS Stake holders- Institutions Involved in HIV/AIDS Reponses</p>
<p>At the national level, the state policy in the area of HIV/AIDS is implemented through the National Programme on Prevention and Control of HIV/AIDS and STI, which determines national strategies of priority for prevention, epidemiological surveillance and treatment. The structure of the institutional framework of the NAP is rather complex. The main executors of the state policy in the area of HIV/AIDS and STI are the Government, local public administration authorities, Ministry of Health and Social Protection and other Ministries, NGOs, mass media, etc. An important contribution is carried out by international organizations, such as UNAIDS and most UN agencies, GFATM/WB, Soros Foundation Moldova, SIDA, etc.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="association-youth-for-right-to-life-balti">Association "Youth for Right to Life", Balti<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#association-youth-for-right-to-life-balti" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hiv-strains-types-groups-and-subtypes">HIV Strains: Types, Groups and Subtypes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-strains-types-groups-and-subtypes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>HIV types, groups and subtypes</p>
<p>HIV is a highly variable virus which mutates very readily. This means there are many different strains of HIV, even within the body of a single infected person.</p>
<p>Based on genetic similarities, the numerous virus strains may be classified into types, groups and subtypes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-the-difference-between-hiv-1-and-hiv-2">What is the difference between HIV-1 and HIV-2?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-the-difference-between-hiv-1-and-hiv-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two types of HIV: HIV-1 and HIV-2. Both types are transmitted by sexual contact, through blood, and from mother to child, and they appear to cause clinically indistinguishable AIDS. However, it seems that HIV-2 is less easily transmitted, and the period between initial infection and illness is longer in the case of HIV-2.</p>
<p>Worldwide, the predominant virus is HIV-1, and generally when people refer to HIV without specifying the type of virus they will be referring to HIV-1. The relatively uncommon HIV-2 type is concentrated in West Africa and is rarely found elsewhere.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-many-subtypes-of-hiv-1-are-there">How many subtypes of HIV-1 are there?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-many-subtypes-of-hiv-1-are-there" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The strains of HIV-1 can be classified into four groups: the "major" group M, the "outlier" group O and two new groups, N and P. These four groups may represent four separate introductions of simian immunodeficiency virus into humans.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-1a993d35.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>HIV types, groups and subtypes</p>
<p>Group O appears to be restricted to west-central Africa and group N - a strain discovered in 1998 in Cameroon - is extremely rare. In 2009 a new strain closely relating to gorilla simian immunodeficiency virus was discovered in a Cameroonian woman. It was designated HIV-1 group P. More than 90 percent of HIV-1 infections belong to HIV-1 group M and, unless specified, the rest of this page will relate to HIV-1 group M only.</p>
<p>Within group M there are known to be at least nine genetically distinct subtypes (or clades) of HIV-1. These are subtypes A, B, C, D, F, G, H, J and K.</p>
<p>Occasionally, two viruses of different subtypes can meet in the cell of an infected person and mix together their genetic material to create a new hybrid virus (a process similar to sexual reproduction, and sometimes called "viral sex"). Many of these new strains do not survive for long, but those that infect more than one person are known as "circulating recombinant forms" or CRFs. For example, the CRF A/B is a mixture of subtypes A and B.</p>
<p>The classification of HIV strains into subtypes and CRFs is a complex issue and the definitions are subject to change as new discoveries are made. Some scientists talk about subtypes A1, A2, A3, F1 and F2 instead of A and F, though others regard the former as sub-subtypes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-about-subtypes-e-and-i">What about subtypes E and I?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-about-subtypes-e-and-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One of the CRFs is called A/E because it is thought to have resulted from hybridization between subtype A and some other "parent" subtype E. However, no one has ever found a pure form of subtype E. Confusingly, many people still refer to the CRF A/E as "subtype E" (in fact it is most correctly called CRF01_AE).</p>
<p>A virus isolated in Cyprus was originally placed in a new subtype I, before being reclassified as a recombinant form A/G/I. It is now thought that this virus represents an even more complex CRF</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>69</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>comprised of subtypes A, G, H, K and unclassified regions. The designation "I" is no longer used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="where-are-the-different-subtypes-and-crfs-found">Where are the different subtypes and CRFs found?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#where-are-the-different-subtypes-and-crfs-found" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The HIV-1 subtypes and CRFs are typically associated with certain geographical regions, with the most widespread being subtypes A and C. As studies have shown, individuals are increasingly presenting with sub-types not native to the country of diagnosis. For example, a rise of non-B sub-types among men who have sex with men (MSM) in the UK has been identified.</p>
<ul>
<li>Subtype A and CRF A/G predominate in West and Central Africa, with subtype A possibly also causing much of the Russian epidemic.</li>
<li>Historically, subtype B has been the most common subtype/CRF in Europe, the Americas, Japan and Australia and is the predominant sub-type found among MSM infected in Europe. Although this remains the case, other subtypes are becoming more frequent and now account for at least 25 percent of new HIV infections in Europe.</li>
<li>Subtype C is predominant in Southern and East Africa, India and Nepal. It has caused the world's worst HIV epidemics and is responsible for around half of all infections.</li>
<li>Subtype D is generally limited to East and Central Africa. CRF A/E is prevalent in South-East Asia, but originated in Central Africa. Subtype F has been found in Central Africa, South America and Eastern Europe. Subtype G and CRF A/G have been observed in West and East Africa and Central Europe.</li>
<li>Subtype H has only been found in Central Africa; J only in Central America; and K only in the Democratic Republic of Congo and Cameroon.</li>
</ul>
<p>As a Belgium study highlighted, local epidemics can be better understood if sub-types, patient demographics and transmission routes are recorded. Furthermore, the availability of this data can be used to target risk groups more accurately and to improve the effectiveness of prevention strategies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="are-more-subtypes-likely-to-appear">Are more subtypes likely to "appear"?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#are-more-subtypes-likely-to-appear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is almost certain that new HIV genetic subtypes and CRFs will be discovered in the future, and indeed that new ones will develop as virus recombination and mutation continue to occur. The current subtypes and CRFs will also continue to spread to new areas as the global epidemic continues.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-implications-of-variability">The implications of variability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-implications-of-variability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="does-subtype-affect-disease-progression">Does subtype affect disease progression?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#does-subtype-affect-disease-progression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A study presented in 2006 found that Ugandans infected with subtype D or recombinant strains incorporating subtype D developed AIDS sooner than those infected with subtype A, and also died sooner, if they did not receive antiretroviral treatment. The study's authors suggested that subtype D is more virulent because it is more effective at binding to immune cells. This result was supported by another study presented in 2007, which found that Kenyan women infected with subtype D had more than twice the risk of death over six years compared with those infected with subtype A. An earlier study of sex workers in Senegal, published in 1999, found that women infected with subtype C, D or G were more likely to develop AIDS within five years of infection than those infected with subtype A.</p>
<p>Several studies conducted in Thailand suggest that people infected with CRF A/E progress faster to AIDS and death than those infected with subtype B, if they do not receive antiretroviral treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="are-there-differences-in-transmission">Are there differences in transmission?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#are-there-differences-in-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It has been observed that certain subtypes/CRFs are predominantly associated with specific modes of transmission. In particular, subtype B is spread mostly by homosexual contact and intravenous drug use (essentially via blood), while subtype C and CRF A/E tend to fuel heterosexual epidemics (via a mucosal route).</p>
<p>Whether there are biological causes for the observed differences in transmission routes remains the subject of debate. Some scientists, such as Dr Max Essex of Harvard, believe such causes do exist. Among their claims are that subtype C and CRF A/E are transmitted much more efficiently during heterosexual sex than subtype B. However, this theory has not been conclusively proven. More recent studies have looked for variation between subtypes in rates of mother-to-child transmission. One of these found that such transmission is more common with subtype D than subtype A. Another reached the opposite conclusion (A worse than D), and also found that subtype C was more often transmitted that subtype D. A third study concluded that subtype C is more transmissible than either D or A. Other researchers have found no association between subtype and rates of mother-to-child transmission.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>6</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Is it possible to be infected more than once?</p>
<p>Until about 1994, it was generally thought that individuals do not become infected with multiple distinct HIV-1 strains. Since then, many cases of people coinfected with two or more strains have been documented.</p>
<p>All cases of confection were once assumed to be the result of people being exposed to the different strains more or less simultaneously, before their immune systems had had a chance to react. However, it is now thought that "superinfection" is also occurring. In these cases, the second infection occurred several months after the first. It would appear that the body's immune response to the first virus is sometimes not enough to prevent infection with a second strain, especially with a virus belonging to a different subtype. It is not yet known how commonly super infection occurs, or whether it can take place only in special circumstances.</p>
<p>Do HIV antibody tests detect all types, groups and subtypes?</p>
<p>Initial tests for HIV are usually conducted using the EIA (or ELISA) antibody test or a rapid antibody test.</p>
<p>Compared with first generation EIA antibody tests that were initially developed, third and fourth generation EIA antibody tests are significantly more accurate. Unlike previous tests, the fourth generation test detects HIV antibodies and antigens simultaneously. The WHO recommends that tests should have an accuracy rate of 99 percent and whilst most do, this may vary slightly between the test brands.</p>
<p>The most-up-to date (fourth generation) EIA tests detect both HIV-1 and HIV-2 infections. Although most HIV infections are HIV-1 group M, EIA tests are also able to detect infections with rare groups and subtypes.</p>
<p>However, as HIV-2 and group O infections are extremely rare in most countries, routine screening programs might not be designed to test for them. Anyone who believes they may have contracted HIV-2, HIV-1 group O or one of the rarer subtypes of group M should seek expert advice.</p>
<p>What are the treatment implications?</p>
<p>An HIV positive man sitting at home before taking his antiretroviral drugs</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Although most current HIV-1 antiretroviral drugs were designed for use against subtype B, there is no compelling evidence that they are any less effective against other subtypes. Nevertheless, some subtypes may be more likely to develop resistance to certain drugs, and the types of mutations associated with resistance may vary. This is an important subject for future research. The effectiveness of HIV-1 treatment is monitored using viral load tests. It has been demonstrated that some viral load tests are sensitive only to subtype B and can produce a significant underestimate of viral load if used to process other strains. The latest tests do claim to produce accurate results for most Group M subtypes, though not necessarily for Group O. It is important that health workers and patients are aware of the subtype/CRF they are testing for and of the limitations of the test they are applying.</p>
<p>Not all of the drugs used to treat HIV-1 infection are as effective against HIV-2. In particular, HIV-2 has a natural resistance to NNRTI antiretroviral drugs and they are therefore not recommended. As yet there is no FDA-licensed viral load test for HIV-2 and those designed for HIV-1 are not reliable for monitoring the other type. Instead, response to treatment may be monitored by following CD4+ T-cell counts and indicators of immune system deterioration. More research and clinical experience is needed to determine the most effective treatment for HIV-2.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-implications-for-an-aids-vaccine">What are the implications for an AIDS vaccine?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-implications-for-an-aids-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The development of an AIDS vaccine is affected by the range of virus subtypes as well as by the wide variety of human populations who need protection and who differ, for example, in their genetic make-up and their routes of exposure to HIV. In particular, the occurrence of super infection indicates that an immune response triggered by a vaccine to prevent infection by one strain of HIV may not protect against all other strains. The increasing variety of sub-types found within countries suggests that the effectiveness of a vaccine is likely to vary between populations, unless an innovative method is developed which guards against many virus strains. Inevitably, different types of candidate vaccines will have to be tested against various viral strains in multiple vaccine trials, conducted in both high-income and developing countries</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="opportunistic-infections">OPPORTUNISTIC INFECTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opportunistic-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>

<li>TESTING FOR OIs</li>

</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-opportunistic-infections">WHAT ARE OPPORTUNISTIC INFECTIONS?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-opportunistic-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In our bodies, we carry many germs – bacteria, protozoa, fungi, and viruses. When our immune system is working, it controls these germs. But when the immune system is weakened by HIV disease or by some medications, these germs can get out of control and cause health problems. Infections that take advantage of weakness in the immune defenses are called “opportunistic”. The phrase “opportunistic infection” is often shortened to “OI”.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="testing-for-ois">TESTING FOR OIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#testing-for-ois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You can be infected with an OI, and “test positive” for it, even though you don’t have the disease. For example, almost everyone with HIV tests positive for Cytomegalovirus (CMV). But it is very rare for CMV disease to develop unless the CD4 cell count drops below 50, a sign of serious damage to the immune system.</p>
<p>To see if you’re infected with an OI, your blood might be tested for antigens (pieces of the germ that causes the OI) or for antibodies (proteins made by the immune system to fight the germs). If the antigens are found, it means you’re infected. If the antibodies are found, you’ve been exposed to the infection. You may have been immunized against the infection, or your immune system may have? cleared? the infection, or you may be infected. If you are infected with a germ that causes an OI, and if your CD4 cells are low enough to allow that OI to develop, your health care provider will look for signs of active disease. These are different for the different OIs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ois-and-aids">OIs AND AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ois-and-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>People who aren’t HIV-infected can develop OIs if their immune systems are damaged. For example, many drugs used to treat cancer suppress the immune system. Some people who get cancer treatments can develop OIs.</p>
<p>HIV weakens the immune system so that opportunistic infections can develop. If you are HIV-infected and develop opportunistic infections, you might have AIDS.</p>
<p>In the US, the Center for Disease Control (CDC) is responsible for deciding who has AIDS. The CDC has developed a list of about 24 opportunistic infections. If you have HIV and one or more</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>of these “official” OIs, then you have AIDS. The list is available at <a href="http://www.aidsmeds.com/lessons/StartHere8.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.aidsmeds.com/lessons/StartHere8.htm</a>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-most-common-ois">WHAT ARE THE MOST COMMON OIs?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-most-common-ois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the early years of the AIDS epidemic, OIs caused a lot of sickness and deaths. Once people started taking strong antiretroviral therapy (ART), however, a lot fewer people got OIs. It’s not clear how many people with HIV will get a specific OI.</p>
<p>In women, health problems in the vaginal area may be early signs of HIV. These can include pelvic inflammatory disease and bacterial vaginosis, among others. See fact sheet 610 for more information.</p>
<p>The most common OIs are listed here, along with the disease they usually cause, and the CD4 cell count when the disease becomes active:</p>
<ul>
<li>Candidiasis (Thrush) is a fungal infection of the mouth, throat, or vagina. CD4 cell range: can occur even with fairly high CD4 cells.</li>
<li>Cytomegalovirus (CMV) is a viral infection that causes eye disease that can lead to blindness. CD4 cell range: under 50.</li>
<li>Herpes simplex viruses can cause oral herpes (cold sores) or genital herpes. These are fairly common infections, but if you have HIV, the outbreaks can be much more frequent and more severe. They can occur at any CD4 cell count.</li>
<li>Malaria is common in the developing world. It is more common and more severe in people with HIV infection.</li>
<li>Mycobacterium avium complex (MAC or MAI) is a bacterial infection that can cause recurring fevers, general sick feelings, problems with digestion, and serious weight loss. CD4 cell range: under 75.</li>
<li>Pneumocystis pneumonia (PCP) is a fungal infection that can cause a fatal pneumonia. CD4 cell range: under 200. Unfortunately this is still a fairly common OI in people who have not been tested or treated for HIV.</li>
<li>Toxoplasmosis (Toxo) is a protozoal infection of the brain. T-cell range: under 100.</li>
<li>Tuberculosis (TB) is a bacterial infection that attacks the lungs, and can cause meningitis. CD4 cell range: Everyone with HIV who tests positive for exposure to TB should be treated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventing-ois">PREVENTING OIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventing-ois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Most of the germs that cause OIs are quite common, and you may already be carrying several of these infections. You can reduce the risk of new infections by keeping clean and avoiding known sources of the germs that cause OIs.</p>
<p>Even if you're infected with some OIs, you can take medications that will prevent the development of active disease. This is called prophylaxis. The best way to prevent OIs is to take strong ART. See Fact Sheet 403 for more information on ART.</p>
<p>The Fact Sheets for each OI have more information on avoiding infection or preventing the development of active disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treating-ois">TREATING OIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treating-ois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For each OI, there are specific drugs, or combinations of drugs, that seem to work best. Refer to the Fact Sheets for each OI to learn more about how they are treated.</p>
<p>Strong antiretroviral drugs can allow a damaged immune system to recover and do a better job of fighting OIs. Fact Sheet 481 on Immune Restoration has more information on this topic</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>HIV infection weakens your immune system, making you highly susceptible to numerous infections and certain types of cancers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infections-common-to-hiv-aids">Infections common to HIV/AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infections-common-to-hiv-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Tuberculosis (TB). In resource-poor nations, TB is the most common opportunistic infection associated with HIV and a leading cause of death among people with AIDS. Millions of people are currently infected with both HIV and tuberculosis, and many experts consider the two diseases to be twin epidemics.</li>
<li>Salmonellosis. You contract this bacterial infection from contaminated food or water. Signs and symptoms include severe diarrhea, fever, chills, abdominal pain and, occasionally, vomiting. Although anyone exposed to salmonella bacteria can become sick, salmonellosis is far more common in HIV-positive people.</li>
<li>Cytomegalovirus. This common herpes virus is transmitted in body fluids such as saliva, blood, urine, semen and breast milk. A healthy immune system inactivates the virus, and it remains dormant in your body. If your immune system weakens, the virus resurfaces — causing damage to your eyes, digestive tract, lungs or other organs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Candidiasis. Candidiasis is a common HIV-related infection. It causes inflammation and a thick, white coating on the mucous membranes of your mouth, tongue, esophagus or vagina. Children may have especially severe symptoms in the mouth or esophagus, which can make eating painful.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cryptococcal meningitis. Meningitis is an inflammation of the membranes and fluid surrounding your brain and spinal cord (meninges). Cryptococcal meningitis is a common central nervous system infection associated with HIV, caused by a fungus found in soil. The disease may also be associated with bird or bat droppings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Toxoplasmosis. This potentially deadly infection is caused by Toxoplasma gondii, a parasite spread primarily by cats. Infected cats pass the parasites in their stools, and the parasites may then spread to other animals and humans.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cryptosporidiosis. This infection is caused by an intestinal parasite that's commonly found in animals. You contract cryptosporidiosis when you ingest contaminated food or water. The parasite grows in your intestines and bile ducts, leading to severe, chronic diarrhea in people with AIDS.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cancers-common-to-hiv-aids">Cancers common to HIV/AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancers-common-to-hiv-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Kaposi's sarcoma. A tumor of the blood vessel walls, this cancer is rare in people not infected with HIV, but common in HIV-positive people.</li>
</ul>
<p>Kaposi's sarcoma usually appears as pink, red or purple lesions on the skin and mouth. In people with darker skin, the lesions may look dark brown or black. Kaposi's sarcoma can also affect the internal organs, including the digestive tract and lungs.</p>
<ul>
<li>Lymphomas. This type of cancer originates in your white blood cells and usually first appears in your lymph nodes. The most common early sign is painless swelling of the lymph nodes in your neck, armpit or groin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-complications">Other complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wasting syndrome. Aggressive treatment regimens have reduced the number of cases of wasting syndrome, but it still affects many people with AIDS. It's defined as a loss of at least 10 percent of body weight, often accompanied by diarrhea, chronic weakness and fever.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Neurological complications. Although AIDS doesn't appear to infect the nerve cells, it can cause neurological symptoms such as confusion, forgetfulness, depression, anxiety and difficulty walking. One of the most common neurological complications is AIDS dementia complex, which leads to behavioral changes and diminished mental functioning.</li>
<li>Kidney disease. HIV-associated nephropathy (HIVAN) is an inflammation of the tiny filters in your kidneys that remove excess fluid and wastes from your bloodstream and pass them to your urine. Because of a genetic predisposition, the risk of developing HIVAN is much higher in blacks.</li>
</ul>
<p>Regardless of CD4 count, antiretroviral therapy should be started in those diagnosed with HIVAN.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-8abe4237.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-a0ebec79.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9bace7b1">AIDS Stakeholders – Institutions Involved in HIV/AIDS Response in Moldova<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9bace7b1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the national level, the state policy in the area of HIV/AIDS is implemented through the National Programme on Prevention and Control of HIV/AIDS and STI, which determines national strategies of priority for prevention, epidemiological surveillance and treatment. The structure of the institutional framework of the NAP is rather complex. The main executors of the state policy in the area of HIV/AIDS and STI are the Government, local public administration authorities, Ministry of Health and Social Protection and other Ministries, NGOs, mass media, etc. An important contribution is carried out by international organizations, such as UNAIDS and most UN agencies, GFATM/WB, Soros Foundation Moldova, SIDA, etc.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>National AIDS Stakeholders and their Role</p>
<p><strong>National Coordination Council and NCC Secretariat</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Development, integration, correlation and monitoring of activities under the NAP</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Government and its Ministries</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Capacity building related to national response to HIV/AIDS/STI;</li>
<li>Support to the consolidation of NGO networks which are working in the field of HIV/AIDS/STI and people living with HIV/AIDS;</li>
<li>Priority financing, political support of HIV/AIDS activities;</li>
<li>Focal points and HIV related responsibilities under several ministries;</li>
<li>M&amp;E</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Local Public Administration Authorities</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Regional interdepartmental, multisectoral HIV/AIDS/STIs committees;</li>
<li>Earmarking in local budgets for HIV/AIDS activities;</li>
<li>Contribution to regional programmes in the field.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Mass Media</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Promote and make use of non-discriminatory language in HIV/AIDS/STIs</li>
<li>Communication activities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>National Centre for Public Health</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Evaluation of population health, prognosis as to the evolution of basic indicators and sanitary-epidemiological statistics;</li>
<li>Elaboration of prevention programmes at national and territorial levels;</li>
<li>Fighting negative effect of harmful environment and production factors;</li>
<li>Cooperation with other medical-sanitary national and international institutions of common and global interest;</li>
<li>Exchange of experience and information.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Public Institution "UCIMP"</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Strengthening of the public health through reforming the health system;</li>
<li>Development of the institutional capacities;</li>
<li>Fighting negative effect of harmful environment and production factors;</li>
</ul>
