<p>COMMUNICABLE DISEASES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="terms">TERMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Communicable diseases - An illness due to specific infections agent or its toxic product which arise through transmission of the agent or its toxin form a reservoir susceptible host either directly, indirectly as an infected animals or person or indirectly through the agency of intermediate plant or animals host vector or in animate environment.</p>
<p>☑ Infection - Invasion of the body by dx causing organism.</p>
<p>☑ Cross infection - Normally occurs in the hospital btn patient due to their cross proximity or carelessness of the staff.</p>
<p>☑ Drop infection - Organism are spread by minute particle of moisture especially in coughing or sneezing.</p>
<p>☑ Mass infection - Infection of the blood extremely large no. of the organism.</p>
<p>☑ Secondary infection - Prefers to the super-imposed second infection that occurs while one is already present i.e. re-infection</p>
<p>☑ Incubation period - Is the time taken from the time of infection 2 the time the signs and symptoms of illness appear.</p>
<p>☑ Clinical infection - Where the organism or agent produce signs &amp; symptoms.</p>
<p>☑ Sub-clinical infection (Asymptomatic) - This is where the sign &amp; symptoms are not showed up clear. There is no usual clinical diagnosis.</p>
<p>☑ Health carrier - A person carrying diseases, agent but is not affected but can transmit it to other person.</p>
<p>☑ Susceptible host - Refer to one who has no or has less resistance to disease or infection.</p>
<p>☑ Host - The organism, man or animals on which a parasite lives &amp; multiplies.</p>
<p>☑ Intermediate host - One that shelter parasite during the non-productive period (larval stage)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Pandemic-This is when a disease spread in many countries through the world.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Epidemic-When a disease spreads out attacking a large no. of people. It's a rapid outbreak of diseases.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Endemic – A term used to describe any disease prevalent in a particular area.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Sporadic – Refers to a disease occurring here and there (scattered).
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Incidence- Refers to new cases occurring at a particular time in a place.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Fatality- Death due to a certain disease.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> ……</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Most of the common diseases in Africa are environmental diseases and are due to infection by living organisms which are viruses, bacteria, Chlamydia, ricketsiae, fungi, protozoa, metazoan or Helminthes. These are called communicable diseases because they spread from person to person or from animals to people. Together with malnutrition they are today the major cause of illness in Africa. The communicable diseases occur at all ages but are most serious in childhood due to an increased intensity of exposure and a poorly developed immunity. These diseases are to a great extent preventable.</p>
<p>In countries where they have been largely eliminated, other conditions such as degenerative and malignant diseases have taken place. This process is known as the Epidemiological transition.</p>
<p>Infections that have increased in incidence during the last couple of decades and whose incidence is predicted to increase in the near future have appeared. They are called “emerging infectious diseases”. The reasons behind these emerging infections are not known but likely factors include:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Societal events</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Economic impoverishment</li>
<li>War or civil conflicts</li>
<li>Population growth and migration</li>
<li>Urban decay</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Health care</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>New medical devices</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
85
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Organ or tissue transplantation</li>
<li>Drugs causing immunosuppression</li>
<li>Widespread use of antibiotics</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Food production</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Globalization of food supplies</li>
<li>Changes in food processing and packaging</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Human behavior</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Sexual behavior</li>
<li>Drug use</li>
<li>Travel</li>
<li>Diet</li>
<li>Outdoor recreation</li>
<li>Use of childcare facilities</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Environmental changes</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Deforestation/reforestation</li>
<li>Changes in water ecosystems</li>
<li>Flood/drought</li>
<li>Famine</li>
<li>Global warming</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Public health</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Curtailment or reduction in preventive programmes</li>
<li>Infrastructure and communicable disease surveillance inadequate</li>
<li>Lack of trained personnel</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Microbial adaptation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Changes in virulence and toxin production</li>
<li>Development and change of drug resistance</li>
<li>Microbes as co-factors in chronic diseases</li>
</ul>
<p>More simplified, the factors to emerging and re-emerging of infections are:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Agricultural practices and consumption of exotic animals-genetic recombination</li>
<li>Change of land use-forest land to agricultural land causing deforestation</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Rapid international travel</li>
<li>Poverty and disease</li>
<li>Urbanization</li>
<li>Forced displacement due to war or civil strife</li>
<li>Human morality and disease</li>
<li>Overuse of antibiotics-resistance</li>
<li>Biblical perspective-unclean animals, unclean environments, sexual immorality e.g. homosexual and lesbians and broken relationship with God.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="communicable-diseases-are-very-important-in-africa-because">Communicable diseases are very important in Africa because:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#communicable-diseases-are-very-important-in-africa-because" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Many of them are very common</li>
<li>Some of them are very serious and cause death and disability</li>
<li>Some come as widespread outbreaks, i.e. epidemics</li>
<li>Many of them are fairly preventable by fairly simple means</li>
<li>Many are particularly serious (and more common) in infants and children.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-broad-classification-of-diseases">I. BROAD CLASSIFICATION OF DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-broad-classification-of-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Metabolic disorders - Chemical and physical processes within the body-disordered biochemistry in the body i.e. cholesterol imbalance e.g. diabetes</li>
<li>Congenital diseases - Mental or physical abnormalities that are present at, and usually before birth, some may be medically insignificant and may not appear for some time. In other cases they may pose a direct threat to life and requires immediate attention. Examples are cataract, cleft palate, cretinism, down's syndrome, congenital heart disease, hemophilia, joints disorders, spinal bifida. Blindness, deafness, hydrocephalus can also be due to congenital disorders.</li>
<li>Hereditary diseases - This is the transmission of mental and physical characteristics from parents to their children, and also the total genetic constitution of any individual. Examples are hemophilia, sickle cell anemia, etc</li>
<li>Allergy diseases - A condition in which the body reacts with unusual sensitivity to a certain substance(s). These substances which are usually proteins are called antigens. They stimulate the body to produce antibodies which weaken or destroy the invading</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>87</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>antigens. In some cases, when an antibody reacts with an antigen, the organic compound histamine is released from special body cells called mast cells. It is an excess of histamine that results in allergy symptoms e.g. hay fever, asthma.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Traumatic diseases-A medical term for an injury, could be physical or psychological e.g. shock, Accident</li>
<li>Nutritional/deficiency diseases-In adequate, lack of essential nutrients e.g. Obesity, marasmus, kwashiorkor, nutritional anemiaetc</li>
<li>Occupational diseases-Diseases associated with one's occupation e.g. silicosis, asbestosis, Lung fibrosis etc</li>
<li>Toxic diseases-Due to contact with toxic substances e.g. poisoning, snake venom, etc</li>
<li>Degenerative diseases-Wear and tear of the body tissues e.g. arthritis, arteriosclerosis, rheumatism,etc</li>
<li>Addictive diseases-Due to desire/urge to use some substances e.g. alcoholism, smoking etc</li>
<li>Mental disorders-Refers to a broad range of psychiatric disorders that reflect a deviation from normal thought and behavior patterns e.g. psychosis, schizophrenia, etc</li>
<li>Neoplastic disorders-The medical name for any abnormal new growth commonly referred to as tumors e.g. cancers</li>
<li>Psychosocial disorders-Refers to a mental illness caused or influenced by life experiences as well as maladjusted cognitive and behavioral processes. They can be due to psychological and social factors that influence mental health. Social influences such as peer pressure, parental support, cultural and religious background, socioeconomic status and interpersonal relationship e.g. juvenile delinquency, rapists, stress etc</li>
<li>Communicable diseases-Diseases spread from one person to another or from animal to person</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-classification-of-communicable-diseases-based-on-how-the-disease-is-transmitted">II. CLASSIFICATION OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASES (BASED ON HOW THE DISEASE IS TRANSMITTED)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-classification-of-communicable-diseases-based-on-how-the-disease-is-transmitted" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Contact diseases-The means of transmission is through:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Skin to skin contact</li>
<li>Direct touch of infected person</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Indirect-handling contaminated articles (fomites) e.g. clothing.</li>
</ul>
<p>They tend to occur in places of:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Overcrowding</li>
<li>Clusters within the family</li>
<li>Children’s playgrounds-schools, etc</li>
<li>Work</li>
</ul>
<p>Communicability occurs in the following situations:-</p>
<ul>
<li>High population density e.g. urban centers</li>
<li>Overcrowding</li>
<li>Poor housing</li>
<li>Close personal contact including sexual contact</li>
<li>Inadequate water supply</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples are scabies, pediculosis, fungal skin infections, candidiasis, trachoma, etc</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Sexually transmitted diseases/infections-Usually transmitted during sexual intercourse hence the name STDs/STIs. During sexual intercourse there is close body contact which is an ideal situation for transmission e.g. gonorrhea, etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vector-borne diseases-The insect vectors usually acquire the disease organisms by sucking blood from infected persons and later pass it on by the same route. There are other transmission routes however. Infection may enter skin cracks or abrasions either from infected insect feces deposited when feeding or from body fluid when an insect is crushed. Examples are malaria, onchocerciasis, etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Feacal contamination diseases-The causative organisms of the diseases in this group are excreted in the stools of infected persons (or less commonly animals). The portal of entry for these diseases is the mouth. Therefore the causative organisms have to pass through the environment from the feces of an infected person to the gastrointestinal tract of a susceptible person. This is known as the faeco-oral transmission route which occurs mostly through contamination of food, water and hands with faeces. Examples are bacillary</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
89
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>dysentery, amoebiasis, viral hepatitis, cholera, enteric fevers, food poisoning, poliomyelitis, etc</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Helminthic diseases - Due to worms. Examples are ascariasis, enterobiasis, etc</li>
<li>Airborne diseases - Can be transmitted through the air. Examples are measles, mumps, chickenpox, whooping cough, meningitis, pneumonia, tuberculosis, common colds, influenza, etc</li>
<li>Animals and their products contact diseases. Examples are rabies, tetanus, anthrax, brucellosis, etc</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-based-on-causative-infectious-agents">CLASSIFICATION BASED ON CAUSATIVE/INFECTIOUS AGENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-based-on-causative-infectious-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bacterial diseases - bacillary dysentery (Shigellosis), cholera, enteric fevers, tetanus, anthrax, brucellosis, meningitis, tuberculosis, leprosy, plague, gonorrhea, etc</li>
<li>Viral diseases - yellow fever, rabies, measles, chickenpox, poliomyelitis, viral hepatitis, mumps, AIDS, etc</li>
<li>Helminthic diseases - Ascariasis, hydatidosis, filariasis, schistosomiasis, taeniasis, dracunculosis, etc</li>
<li>Protozoan diseases - malaria, leishmaniasis, trypanosomiasis, giardiasis, amoebiasis, trichomoniasis</li>
<li>Chlamydia diseases - trachoma, non-gonococci (non-specific) urethritis, etc</li>
<li>Spirochetes diseases - pinta, syphilis, relapsing fever, yaws, etc</li>
<li>Rickettsia diseases - typhus fever, Q-fever, trench fever, scrub typhus, Dengue fever.</li>
<li>Fungal diseases - candidiasis, banalities, Ringworm etc</li>
<li>Mychotic diseases - Otomychisis, Histoplasmosis, Aetinomycosis</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="another-classification">ANOTHER CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#another-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Water washed diseases</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Diarrhea and dysenteries</li>
<li>Scabies and other skin diseases</li>
<li>Trachoma and other eye diseases</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Water borne diseases</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Typhoid fever and paratyphoid fever</li>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Poliomyelitis</li>
<li>Amoebiasis</li>
<li>Hepatitis A</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Water related diseases</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Malaria</li>
<li>Schistosomiasis</li>
<li>Onchocerciasis</li>
<li>Etc</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-contributing-to-spread-of-diseases-determinants-of-diseases">FACTORS CONTRIBUTING TO SPREAD OF DISEASES (DETERMINANTS OF DISEASES)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-contributing-to-spread-of-diseases-determinants-of-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>HOST</th><th>ENVIRONMENT</th><th>AGENT</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Age</td><td>Geographical factors</td><td>Pathogenicity</td></tr><tr><td>Race</td><td>High/low altitude</td><td>Infectivity</td></tr><tr><td>Genetic</td><td>Rainfall patterns</td><td>Virulence</td></tr><tr><td>Knowledge</td><td>Land fertility</td><td>Sensitivity</td></tr><tr><td>Nutrition</td><td>Vegetation</td><td>Morphology</td></tr><tr><td>Sex</td><td>Sanitation</td><td>Type of organism</td></tr><tr><td>Immunity</td><td>Water</td><td>Antigenicity</td></tr><tr><td>Occupation</td><td>Air</td><td>Stage of multiplication</td></tr><tr><td>Behavior</td><td>Vector</td><td>Degree of pathogenicity</td></tr><tr><td>Culture</td><td>Climate</td><td>Dosage</td></tr><tr><td>Religion</td><td>Housing</td><td>Toxicity</td></tr><tr><td>Customs</td><td>Communication</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Socio-economic</td><td>Radiation</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Concurrent illnesses</td><td>Urbanization</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Industrialization</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pattern-of-communicable-diseases-epidemiological-triad">PATTERN OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASES (EPIDEMIOLOGICAL TRIAD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pattern-of-communicable-diseases-epidemiological-triad" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Different diseases are common in different places and at different times. To understand why this is so, we need to consider the living organism of disease (agent), the people they infect (host) and the surrounding in which they live (environment)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-69950a81.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p>The agents need a suitable environment in which to grow and multiply and thus be able to spread and infect another host. If they are not successful in doing this they die out.</p>
<p>Hosts (people) are affected by their environment e.g. they may live in hot and wet climate in which there are many mosquitoes. But people can also change this environment by draining swamps, changing the vegetation and adding competing hosts such as animals. If the balance is shifted against the agent, the disease will be controlled and the number of cases will go down.</p>
<p>When the balance between the agent, the host and the environment is fairly constant, we tend to see approximately the same number of cases of the disease every month. When this happens the disease is said to be ENDEMIC.</p>
<p>When the balance is shifted in favour of the agent (organism), e.g. when many non-immune children have been born in an area since the last measles epidemic, a large number of cases of measles may occur in a short time. This is called an EPIDEMIC. Epidemic diseases occur during certain periods or seasons and cause sudden deaths and much suffering in the community.</p>
<p>In some parts of the country, some disease outbreaks occur only occasionally without a regular pattern. Such diseases are said to be SPORADIC in their occurrence.</p>
<ul>
<li>Predisposing factors are factors which create a state of susceptibility, so that the host becomes vulnerable to the agent or to necessary cause, e.g. age, sex, previous illness.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Enabling factors are those which assist in the development of (or in recovery from) the disease, e.g. housing conditions, socio-economic status</li>
<li>Precipitating factors are those which are associated with immediate exposure to the disease agent or onset of disease, e.g. drinking contaminated water, close contact with open case of pulmonary TB</li>
<li>Reinforcing factors are those which aggravate an already existing disease e.g. malnutrition, repeated exposures, etc</li>
<li>Risk factor is a condition, quality or attribute, the presence of which increases the chances of an individual to have, develop or be adversely affected by a disease process. A risk factor is thus not necessarily the cause of a disease but does increase the probability that a person exposed to the factor may get the disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="85ac98f0">WHAT HAPPENS ONCE AN INFECTING ORGANISM ENTERS A PERSON’S BODY AND CAUSE DISEASE—THE HOST AND INFECTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#85ac98f0" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A person who is invaded by a disease causing micro-organism is called a HOST. An infection occurs when this microorganism begins to reproduce (multiply) and grow. When an organism infects a person, there are three possible stages to consider:</p>
<ul>
<li>Incubation period</li>
<li>Clinical infection</li>
<li>Sub-clinical infection</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incubation-period">INCUBATION PERIOD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incubation-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Is the time between infection and appearance of signs and symptoms of an illness. During the incubation period the host does not realize that she/he has an infection until several days later when detectable signs and symptoms of the illness occur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-infection">CLINICAL INFECTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the period when the host develops detectable signs and symptoms of an illness.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>93</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sub-clinical-infection">SUB-CLINICAL INFECTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sub-clinical-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At this stage, infection does not produce clear signs and symptoms.</p>
<p>It is important for you to understand these stages because people with signs and symptoms are easier to find as they come to our health facilities for treatment. But people with subclinical infections do not know they are infected and hence are a danger to other people. They are also difficult to detect in the general population without special tests. Individuals who suffer from this stage are also likely to infect others as in the case of HIV infection which leads to AIDS after a long period. They are therefore known as CARRIERS.</p>
<p>An individual who develops a clinical or subclinical infection is said to be susceptible to the disease. A susceptible individual is one whose body lacks resistance to the disease. Resistance of the body to a disease occurs due to various immunity mechanisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disease-transmission-cycle">DISEASE TRANSMISSION CYCLE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease-transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Disease causing organisms are living things. Living things need somewhere to live and reproduce. This place may be an animal, insect or the human body and is known as the RESERVOIR of infection. The human being is the main reservoir of most of the communicable diseases that affect man. When an infection spread to a new host, the place, animal or human from which the organisms come from is called the source of infection. The way in which an organism leaves the source (the infected host) and passes to a new susceptible host is called the route of transmission. Each disease causing organism has particular routes which play a large part in how these organisms spread in the community. For example, some organisms are spread through water and food, while others are spread by vectors like mosquitoes and snails. The cycle through which an organism grows, multiplies and spread is called transmission cycle. In some cases, the human beings may be the only host, in which cases the infection spreads directly from person to person e.g. measles. Transmission cycle is made up of:-</p>
<ul>
<li>The source</li>
<li>Transmission route</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Susceptible host</li>
</ul>
<p>SOURCE</p>
<p>This is where the disease causing organisms spread from. It could be an infected person, animal place or object. The reservoir is the source of infection.</p>
<p>TRANSMISSION ROUTE</p>
<p>The main routes of transmission are:-</p>
<p>✓ Direct contact e.g. sexual contact, contact with skin or mucous membranes
✓ Vectors i.eonchocerciasis , malaria
✓ Faecal-oral ,i.e. ingesting food or water contaminated with feces
✓ Airborne</p>
<p>Examples are</p>
<ul>
<li>Measles</li>
<li>Smallpox</li>
<li>Common cold</li>
<li>Streptococci</li>
<li>Tons line</li>
<li>Diphtheria</li>
<li>Whooping cough</li>
<li>Tuberculosis</li>
<li>Meningitis</li>
<li>Influenza</li>
<li>Chickenpox</li>
<li>Mumps</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ Tran placental (mother to fetus)
✓ Blood e.g. .transfusion, surgery, injection
✓ Contact with animals or their products</p>

Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="susceptible-host">SUSCEPTIBLE HOST<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#susceptible-host" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An individual who has low resistance to a particular disease is said to be a susceptible host to that host. There are a number of factors which lower the body's resistance to a disease. Some of the factors are:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Not having met the disease causing organisms before and therefore not having any immunity to it. For example passive immunity against measles is lost at the age of 6-12 months. Therefore if a child comes into contact with the measles virus after this age, he or she may develop the disease</li>
<li>Having a serious illness which suppresses a person's immunity. Such people have a high risk of developing tuberculosis</li>
<li>Malnutrition.</li>
<li>Certain drugs such as those used to treat cancer can lower one's resistance to disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-of-communicable-diseases-control-principles-of-controlling-communicable-diseases-in-the-community">METHODS OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASES CONTROL/PRINCIPLES OF CONTROLLING COMMUNICABLE DISEASES IN THE COMMUNITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-communicable-diseases-control-principles-of-controlling-communicable-diseases-in-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Communicable diseases can be controlled and eradicated from the community. When thinking about the control of diseases it is always good to think of all the possible methods. Very often, one or two methods are more important and sometimes one or other method does not apply at all to a particular disease. The aim of control is to tip the balance against the agent. The control and eradication can be done by:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Attacking the source of the disease causing organism</li>
<li>Interrupting the transmission route</li>
<li>Protecting the susceptible host</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-attacking-the-source">a. ATTACKING THE SOURCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-attacking-the-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are various specific measures which can be used to attack the source of the infecting organism with the aim of eliminating the organism. They include:-</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Treatment of cases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treating the infected person or animal with the appropriate antibiotics that destroy the disease causing organism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treating the carriers and subclinical cases after carrying on screening tests among suspected individuals or groups.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Mass treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>When a high % age of the people is known to have a diseases. It is sometime advisable to treat everybody without checking whether individuals have the disease or not.</li>
<li>Treating specific groups of persons who are at high risks of being infected (mass treatment). This is called <strong>chemoprophylaxis</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Isolation</p>
<ul>
<li>Isolating those persons who are infected with highly infectious diseases such as Ebola, Marburg fever, Lassa fever, so as to prevent the spread of the organism to other healthy people.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Reservoir control</p>
<ul>
<li>Treating sick animals such as cattle suffering from brucellosis, immunizing animals such as cows from anthrax and dogs from rabies, killing animals such as rats to control plague and dogs to prevent rabies, separating humans from animals.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Notification &amp; reports</p>
<ul>
<li>Although these do not directly affect the source. Notification is an essential means of keeping a watch (Surveillance) on the no. of new cases &amp; thereby monitoring the effectiveness of the control programme.</li>
<li>Notifying the local health authorities immediately you suspect a patient is suffering from an infectious disease. Though this does not directly affect the source, it is an essential way of keeping watch on the number of new cases and thereby monitoring the effectiveness of the control programme. (WHO) International notification diseases is Cholera, <strong>Teller fever</strong>, plague, Ebola e.t.c</li>
<li>National ministries of Health also require notification of certain diseases in their own countries e.g. meningococcal meningitis &amp; acute polio.</li>
</ul>
<p>All these are methods of controlling the reservoir.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>97 |</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>If cases can be treated with drugs that destroy the organism, then fewer (or none) are available to spread to new hosts. The effectiveness of treatment as a control measure depends on how many of the cases in the area can be reached and whether the treatment affects the agent's capacity to reproduce.</p>
<p>Treatment is an important method in the control of tuberculosis and leprosy and most sexually transmitted infections.</p>
<p>For treatment to be effective subclinical cases and carriers must also be treated. However, special efforts have to be made to find them first as they do not usually present with any apparent illness, e.g. subclinical infections of cholera, or asymptomatic sexually transmitted infections.</p>
<p>Where a high percentage of the population is known to have a disease, it is sometimes advisable to treat everybody without checking whether individuals have the disease or not. This is called mass treatment and has been used for example, in the treatment of schistosomiasis in children.</p>
<p>Isolation means that the person with the disease is not allowed to come into close contact with other people except those who are looking after him. Therefore the organisms cannot spread. Isolation is used to control highly infectious and serious conditions such as Ebola. (Tuberculosis cases used to be isolated but not anymore, why?). Isolation is very difficult to enforce, and has a number of disadvantages. In particular, people are frightened of being isolated and this stops them coming for treatment and so increases the spread of the disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-interrupting-the-transmission-route">b. INTERRUPTING THE TRANSMISSION ROUTE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-interrupting-the-transmission-route" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A number of methods are used to interrupt the transmission cycle. They include:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Personal hygiene &amp; behavioral changes</li>
<li>Environmental sanitation</li>
<li>Water and sanitation</li>
<li>Vector control</li>
<li>Good and adequate housing</li>
<li>Food handling</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Sterilization of medical equipments and the use of sterile surgical equipments (disinfection &amp; sterilization)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-protecting-the-host">c. PROTECTING THE HOST<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-protecting-the-host" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the third principle of controlling the spread of communicable diseases in the community. Any person who is not yet infected by a specific disease-causing organism is known as a susceptible host. This is because they are at risk of contracting the infection. All susceptible hosts must be protected from contracting the infection. There are various specific and general measures for protecting the host:-</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-measures">Specific measures:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Immunization using vaccines such as the KEPI vaccines</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immunization increases host resistance by strengthening the internal defenses—antibodies, killer cells, etc. It is one of the most effective methods of control for some communicable diseases. Immunization plays a critical role in the control of many diseases in Africa. For example, it was responsible for the worldwide eradication of smallpox. Diseases in Africa which are now being controlled through immunization include measles, polio, whooping cough, diphtheria, tuberculosis, tetanus, hepatitis B and influenza.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Better Nutrition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malnourished children get infections more easily and suffer more severe complications e.g. diarrhoea. Also, infections occur during famine where people crowd together for assistance making it easy for the disease to spread and result in epidemics.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chemoprophylaxis use Drugs that protect the host be used to suppress infection. e.g. paludrine to suppress malaria parasites, tetracycline during cholera outbreaks, and cotrimazole during plague outbreaks.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Personal protection (PPDs)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The spread of some diseases may be limited by use of barrier against infection e.g. shoes to prevent dust &amp; hookworms from soils, use of nets &amp; insect repellant 2 prevent bites e.t.c</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>General measures:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of bed nets and insect repellants to prevent mosquito bites.</li>
<li>Wearing shoes to prevent penetration of hookworm larvae from the soil.</li>
<li>Adequate space/housing to reduce overcrowding.</li>
<li>Improved nutrition.</li>
<li>Adequate lighting and ventilation.</li>
<li>Health education.</li>
</ul>
<p>The most effective way of controlling communicable diseases is to use a combination of methods.</p>
<p>OTHER CONTROL MEASURES</p>
<p>There are other useful measures that can be taken to control spread of communicable diseases. Among the measures is the notification of diseases. Notification requires you to keep watch (surveillance) on the number of new cases in your area of work and to immediately inform the local health authority when you come across a patient suffering from an infectious disease. One of the main reasons for notification is to help the health authorities take measures to confirm your suspicion and to control the spread of the disease. Notification of the infectious communicable diseases is the responsibility of all health care workers. It is also a legal requirement according to the Public Health Act cap.242 sec.8 of the laws of Kenya. Some notification diseases in Kenya include:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Plague</li>
<li>Poliomyelitis</li>
<li>Anthrax</li>
<li>Whooping cough(Pertusis)</li>
<li>Cholera</li>
<li>Diphtheria</li>
<li>Trypanosomiasis</li>
<li>Meningococcal meningitis</li>
<li>Measles</li>
<li>Tuberculosis</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Typhoid fever</li>
<li>Yellow fever</li>
<li>Etc</li>
</ul>
<p>Some diseases spread so quickly that they need international control measures, they include cholera, plague and yellow fever. These diseases are reported by the Ministry of Health (MOH) to the World Health Organization (WHO).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="application-of-communicable-disease-control-nmeasures">APPLICATION OF COMMUNICABLE DISEASE CONTROL NMEASURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application-of-communicable-disease-control-nmeasures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The actual application of the control methods we have just discussed can be undertaken by different groups of people. These are individual and villages, dispensaries and health centers and the district and central ministry.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures-at-individual-and-village-level">CONTROL MEASURES AT INDIVIDUAL AND VILLAGE LEVEL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures-at-individual-and-village-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Completing the immunizations</li>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
<li>Food hygiene and adequate nutrition</li>
<li>Using bed nets and protective wear</li>
<li>Abstaining from casual sex, being faithful to one sexual partner or using condoms</li>
<li>Protecting water supply and using clean water</li>
<li>Digging and using pit latrines</li>
<li>Controlling vectors</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-measures-at-dispensary-and-health-centre-level">CONTROL MEASURES AT DISPENSARY AND HEALTH CENTRE LEVEL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-measures-at-dispensary-and-health-centre-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The healthcare workers should support and encourage their clients and community to establish and sustain community based disease control programmes. In addition the healthcare workers should:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Increase immunization coverage</li>
<li>Participate in vector and reservoir control</li>
<li>Emphasize water protection and purification</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Inspect food, markets and eating places</li>
<li>Encourage sanitation and refuse disposal</li>
<li>Promote health and prevent diseases using information, education and communication (IEC)</li>
<li>Notify diseases</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="malaria">MALARIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def: An acute infection of the blood with plasmodium parasite characterized by chills fever, pyrexia, nausea and anorexis.</p>
<p>Aetiological agent- A protozoan of genus plasmodium</p>
<p>4 species are implicated ; these are</p>
<ul>
<li>P. falciparum-12 days</li>
<li>P. vivax-14 days</li>
<li>P. ovale-14 days</li>
<li>P. malariae-30 days</li>
</ul>
<p>NB Incubation period is reduced if transmission is by inoculation through blood transfusion.</p>
<p>Occurrence: Appear either as hypo endemic (low transmission) especially during the day season hyper endemic (some incidents) throughout.</p>
<p>Distribution: Equatorial &amp; humid tropical region with low activities (16°C-21°C)</p>
<p>Susceptibility &amp; Resistance: All susceptible through people living in endemic region tend 2 acquire partial immunity (tolerance due to development of antibodies)</p>
<p>Reservoir: Man</p>
<p>Source: Infected female anopheline mosquito.</p>
<p>Pathogenicity: Occurs in two phases i.e</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Schizogony (sexual)
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Sporogony (a sexual) forms in the blood cell</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-sexual-form-schizogony">1. SEXUAL FORM (schizogony)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-sexual-form-schizogony" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The mosquito picks gametocytes from the human blood during its feeding process. Fertilization of female &amp; male gametocytes take place 2 form zygote; they penetrate mosquito stomach wall &amp; change into cyst which multiply &amp; change into cyst which multiply into sporozoite, that burst through the wall enter the salivary gland.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-a-sexual-form-sporogony">2. A SEXUAL FORM (Sporogony)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-a-sexual-form-sporogony" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sporozoites are introduced into the body by a bite of a mosquito. They enter into the liver, multiply, develop R.B.C which multiply by binary fission and burst the rest cells realizing them as gametocytes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-picture">CLINICAL PICTURE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-cold-stage">1. COLD STAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-cold-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Temp rises but the patient shivers red B.C are bursting (lasts for 1-2 hours)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-hot-stage">2. HOT STAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-hot-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>First-Aid is the assistance given to a person suffering from sudden illness or injury, with care to preserved life, prevent the condition from worsening and promote recovery. It includes initial interventions in a serious condition prior to professional medical help being available.</p>
<p>Interventions include performing CPR (Cardiopulmonary resuscitation) while awaiting an ambulance and complete treatments for minor conditions such as applying a plaster to a cut.</p>
<p>First-Aid is generally performed by the lay person with many people trained in providing basic levels of First-Aid and others willing to do so from acquired knowledge.</p>
<p>Mental Health is an extension of the concept of first aid to cover mental health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims-of-first-aid">Aims of first aid.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims-of-first-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The key aims of first aid are;</p>
<p>I. <strong>Preserve life</strong>: The aim of all medical care which include first aid it to save life and minimize deaths.</p>
<p>II. <strong>Prevent further harm</strong>. This is also called prevent condition from worsening or danger from further injury. This covers external factors such as moving away from the cause of harm and applying pressure to stop bleeding from becoming dangerous.</p>
<p>III. <strong>Promote recovery</strong>. First-Aid also require trying to start the recovery process from the illness or injury and in some cases it might invoke completing a treatment such as applying plaster to a small wound.</p>
<p>Certain skills are considered essential to provision of First-Aid. Particularly the ABC (Airway, Breathing, Circulation.) which focuses on critical lifesaving.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-disciplines">Specific disciplines.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-disciplines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several types of first Aid and First-Aider which may require specific additional training. These are usually undertaken to fulfill the demands of the work or activity undertaken.</p>
<p>I. <strong>Aquatic/marine first aid</strong>. This is usually practiced by professional such as lifeguards. Professional marine, or in a diver rescue and covers a specific problems which may be faced after water based rescue.</p>
<p>II. <strong>Battlefield first aid</strong>. It takes into account the specific need of treating wounded combatants and non-combatants (person or nation engaged in fighting war.) during armed conflict.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>III. Oxygen first aid. This is the provision of First-Aid under conditions where the arrival of emergency responders or the evacuation of the injured person may be delayed due to constraints of terrain, weather, and available persons or equipment. It may be necessarily to care for a person for several hours.</p>
<p>IV. Mental health first aid. It is taught independently of physical first aid on how to support someone experiencing mental health problems or in a crisis situation. It also involves how to identify the first signs of someone developing mental ill health and guides a person to appropriate help.</p>
<p><strong>Symbols.</strong></p>
<p>The internationally accepted symbol for first aid is the white cross on a green background.</p>
<p><strong>Conditions that require first Aid.</strong></p>
<p>I. Altitude sickness. It may begin in a susceptible people at altitude as low as 5000 can cause potentially fatal.</p>
<p>II. Anaphylaxis. This is a life threatening condition in which the airway can become constricted and the patient may go into shock. This reaction may be caused by allergic reactions to allergens such as insect bites. It is treated with injections of epinephrine.</p>
<p>III. Battlefield. It refers to treating gunshots, burns, bone fracture.</p>
<p>IV. Cardiac Arrest. This may lead to death unless a CPR is started within minutes. There is no time to wait for the emergency services to arrive as 92% of people die before reaching the hospital.</p>
<p>V. Chocking. This is blockage of airway which can result to death due to lack of oxygen if the patient's trachea is not cleared. For example by Heimlich maneuver.</p>
<p>VI. Childbirth.</p>
<p>VII. Cramps. This occurs due to accumulation of lactic acid in muscles caused by either inadequate oxygenation of muscles or lack of water or salt.</p>
<p>VIII. Road accidents, drowning or asphyxiation.</p>
<p>IX. Heat stroke (hypothermia)</p>
<p>X. Heavy bleeding</p>
<p>XI. Hyperglycemia and hypoglycemia.</p>
<p>XII. Insects and animal bites.</p>

<p><strong>First-Aid kit.</strong>
Many accidents can happen at home, office, school, laboratories, which require immediate attention before the patient is attend to by a doctor.</p>
<p><strong>Contents of first aid.</strong>
First-Aid manual, adhesive tape, adhesive bandage, elastic bandages, a splint, antiseptic wipes, soap, antibiotic ointment, antiseptic solution (hydrogen peroxide), acetaminophen and ibuprofen, extra prescribed medication, tweezers, sharp scissors, safety pins, disposable instant cold PP, calming lotion, alcohol wipes, thermometer, tooth preservation kit, plastic and nonlatex gloves, flashlight and extra batteries, thermal shock blanket, First-Aid card (contains emergency personal information, phone number, medication, manual)</p>
<p>First aid is the initial assistance or treatment given to a person who is injured or suddenly becomes ill. The person who provides this help may be a first aider, a first responder, a policeman or fireman, or a paramedic or EMT. This chapter prepares you for being a first aider, psychologically and emotionally, as well as giving practical advice on what you should and should not do in an emergency situation.</p>
<p>The information given throughout this book will help you give effective first aid to any casualty in any situation. However, to become a fully competent first aider, you should complete a recognized first aid course and receive certification. This will also strengthen your skills and increase your confidence. The American Red Cross and the American Heart Association teach a variety of first aid courses, at different educational levels.</p>
<p><strong>Aims and objectives</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>To understand your own abilities and limitations.</li>
<li>To stay safe and calm at all times.</li>
<li>To assess a situation quickly and calmly and summon the appropriate help if necessary.</li>
<li>To assist the casualty and provide the necessary treatment, with the help of others if possible.</li>
</ul>
